# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Generate VS Code Diagnostic API Reference Documentation

## Objective

Generate comprehensive API reference documentation for the **VS Code Diagnostic API**. The Diagnostic API allows extensions to report code issues (errors, warnings, information, hints) to users within the editor.

## Scope

Your documentation should cover the following API surface within the `vscode.languages` namespace:

### Core Interfaces and Classes

1. **Diagnostic class**: Represents a single diagnostic (error, warning, info, hint)
2. **DiagnosticCollection interface**: Container for managing diagnostics across documents
3. **DiagnosticSeverity enum**: Severity levels (Error, Warning, Information, Hint)
4. **DiagnosticRelatedInformation class**: Additional context for diagnostics
5. **DiagnosticTag enum**: Tags for categorizing diagnostics (Unnecessary, Deprecated)

### Key Functions

1. **createDiagnosticCollection()**: Factory function for creating diagnostic collections
2. **getDiagnostics()**: Retrieve diagnostics for a resource or workspace

### Events

1. **onDidChangeDiagnostics**: Event fired when diagnostics change globally

## Required Content

Your API reference must include:

### For Each API Method/Function:
- **Signature**: Full TypeScript signature with parameter types and return type
- **Parameters**: Description of each parameter, including optional/required status
- **Return value**: Description of what is returned
- **Behavior notes**: How the API behaves in different scenarios
- **Error cases**: What errors can occur and when

### For Each Interface/Class:
- **Properties**: All properties with types and descriptions
- **Methods**: All methods with signatures and behavior
- **Constructor**: Construction pattern (if applicable)
- **Lifecycle**: Object lifecycle and disposal semantics

### Usage Examples:
- **Basic usage**: Simple diagnostic creation and publishing
- **Advanced patterns**: Event subscription, cleanup, related information
- **Real-world patterns**: Extract usage examples from internal VS Code code

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` using Markdown format.

You may choose any clear structure as long as all required sections are covered:

```
# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference

## Overview
[Brief introduction to the Diagnostic API]

## Core Types

### Diagnostic
[Class documentation]

### DiagnosticCollection
[Interface documentation]

### DiagnosticSeverity
[Enum documentation]

### DiagnosticRelatedInformation
[Class documentation]

### DiagnosticTag
[Enum documentation]

## Functions

### createDiagnosticCollection()
[Function documentation]

### getDiagnostics()
[Function documentation]

## Events

### onDidChangeDiagnostics
[Event documentation]

## Usage Examples

### Basic Example
[Code example with explanation]

### Advanced Example
[Code example with explanation]

## Common Patterns
[Patterns discovered from internal usage]

## Error Handling
[Error cases and handling strategies]
```

## Tips

- Use the VS Code repository's TypeScript definitions (src/vs/vscode.d.ts) to find exact API signatures
- Search for internal usage in src/vs/workbench/ and extensions/ directories to discover real-world patterns
- Include behavioral notes that aren't obvious from type signatures (e.g., disposal requirements, threading considerations)
- Document the relationship between DiagnosticCollection.set() and getDiagnostics()
- Explain when onDidChangeDiagnostics fires and what information it provides

## Evaluation

Your documentation will be scored on:
- **API completeness** (40%): Coverage of all required API methods, properties, and types
- **Behavioral notes** (30%): Correct description of non-obvious behaviors, lifecycle, error cases
- **Usage examples** (20%): Quality and correctness of code examples from internal callers
- **Structure** (10%): Organization, clarity, and completeness of documentation structure

- 6 common patterns derived from real codebase patterns

  "content": "# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe VS Code Diagnostic API enables extensions to report code issues\u2014errors, warnings, informational messages, and hints\u2014to users within the editor. Diagnostics appear as underlined text in the editor, as entries in the Problems panel, and in the gutter. They are scoped to a specific document URI and managed through diagnostic collections, which group diagnostics by the owning extension or tool.\n\nThe primary entry point is the `vscode.languages` namespace, which provides factory functions and events for working with diagnostics.\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### `Diagnostic`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nRepresents a single diagnostic (error, warning, info, or hint) that applies to a specific range within a document. `Diagnostic` objects are only valid within the scope of a file and must be published via a `DiagnosticCollection` to be visible.\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nconstructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type                | Required | Description |\n|------------|---------------------|----------|-------------|\n| `range`    | `Range`             | Yes      | The range in the document to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid `Range`; throws `TypeError` if not. |\n| `message`  | `string`            | Yes      | The human-readable message to display. Must be non-empty; throws `TypeError` if falsy. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity`| No       | The severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n\n**Error cases:** The constructor throws `TypeError` if `range` is not a valid `Range` or if `message` is empty/falsy.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property             | Type                                                                          | Description |\n|----------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------|\n| `range`              | `Range`                                                                       | The document range the diagnostic applies to. |\n| `message`            | `string`                                                                      | The human-readable diagnostic message. |\n| `severity`           | `DiagnosticSeverity`                                                          | Severity level; defaults to `Error`. |\n| `source`             | `string \\| undefined`                                                         | Optional human-readable source name, e.g. `'typescript'` or `'eslint'`. Used to identify the originating tool in the Problems panel. |\n| `code`               | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri } \\| undefined`  | Optional code or identifier. When an object form is used, `target` is a URI opened when the user clicks the diagnostic code for more information. |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[] \\| undefined`                                 | Optional array of related locations and messages (e.g., other definitions of a duplicate symbol). |\n| `tags`               | `DiagnosticTag[] \\| undefined`                                                | Optional metadata tags that affect rendering (e.g., fading out unnecessary code). |\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- A `Diagnostic` instance has no visual effect until it is added to a `DiagnosticCollection` via `set()`.\n- The `range` does not have to be non-empty; a zero-length range (a cursor position) is valid.\n- `null` diagnostic values inside an array passed to `DiagnosticCollection.set()` are silently coalesced (filtered out).\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticCollection`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nA container that manages a named set of diagnostics across multiple document URIs. Created exclusively via `languages.createDiagnosticCollection()`. Implements `Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]>`, so it can be iterated with `for...of`.\n\nEach diagnostic collection is associated with a single owning extension. Diagnostics from different collections for the same URI are aggregated when calling `languages.getDiagnostics()`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type     | Description |\n|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `name`   | `string` (readonly) | The collection name, set at creation time. Every diagnostic from this collection is associated with this name. Also used by the task framework for problem matchers. Throws if accessed after `dispose()`. |\n\n#### Methods\n\n##### `set(uri, diagnostics)`\n\n```typescript\nset(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n```\n\nAssigns diagnostics for a single resource, replacing all existing diagnostics for that URI.\n\n| Parameter     | Type                                | Description |\n|---------------|-------------------------------------|-------------|\n| `uri`         | `Uri`                               | The resource to update. |\n| `diagnostics` | `readonly Diagnostic[] \\| undefined`| New diagnostics, or `undefined` to remove all diagnostics for that URI (equivalent to `delete(uri)`). |\n\n##### `set(entries)`\n\n```typescript\nset(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n```\n\nReplaces diagnostics for multiple resources in one call.\n\n| Parameter | Type | Description |\n|-----------|------|-------------|\n| `entries` | `ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] \\| undefined]>` | Array of `[uri, diagnostics]` tuples. |\n\n**Merge semantics:** Multiple tuples with the same URI are merged. For example, `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` is equivalent to `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`. A `undefined` diagnostics entry (e.g., `[file1, undefined]`) clears all diagnostics accumulated for `file1` up to that point in the array, but subsequent tuples for the same URI can still add diagnostics.\n\n**Behavior notes:**\n- Calling `set()` always fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` for the affected URIs, even if the diagnostic content has not actually changed.\n- `null` entries within a diagnostics array are silently filtered out.\n- There is a per-file limit (1000 diagnostics) and a total limit (~1100 diagnostics). When a file exceeds the per-file limit, diagnostics are prioritized by severity (Errors first, then Warnings, then Information, then Hints), and an additional informational marker is appended indicating how many diagnostics were omitted.\n- Throws `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `delete(uri)`\n\n```typescript\ndelete(uri: Uri): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics for the given URI from this collection. Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `clear()`\n\n```typescript\nclear(): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics from this collection for every URI. Equivalent to calling `set(undefined)`.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `forEach(callback, thisArg?)`\n\n```typescript\nforEach(\n  callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n  thisArg?: any\n): void\n```\n\nIterates over each URI/diagnostics entry in this collection.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `get(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nget(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n```\n\nReturns the diagnostics for the given URI, or `undefined` if none exist.\n\n**Important:** The returned array is immutable (frozen). Attempting to mutate it (e.g., `push`, `pop`, index assignment) throws a `TypeError`. To modify diagnostics, create a new array and call `set()` again.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `has(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nhas(uri: Uri): boolean\n```\n\nReturns `true` if this collection contains any diagnostics for the given URI.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `dispose()`\n\n```typescript\ndispose(): void\n```\n\nDisposes the collection and frees associated resources. Internally calls `clear()`, removing all diagnostics from the editor. Calling `dispose()` a second time is safe (no-op). After disposal, all other methods throw `Error: illegal state - object is disposed`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticSeverity`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nEnum representing the severity level of a diagnostic. Controls how the diagnostic is rendered in the editor and Problems panel.\n\n| Member        | Value | Description |\n|---------------|-------|-------------|\n| `Error`       | `0`   | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Rendered with a red underline by default. |\n| `Warning`     | `1`   | Something suspicious but allowed. Rendered with a yellow underline by default. |\n| `Information` | `2`   | Something to inform about but not a problem. |\n| `Hint`        | `3`   | A suggestion for a better approach (e.g., proposing a refactoring). Rendered subtly. |\n\n**Priority ordering:** When per-file diagnostic limits are reached, diagnostics are preserved in order: `Error` > `Warning` > `Information` > `Hint`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticRelatedInformation`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nRepresents a related message and source location for a diagnostic. Used to point to code locations that cause or are related to the diagnostic, such as all definitions of a duplicated symbol.\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nconstructor(location: Location, message: string)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type       | Description |\n|------------|------------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The file and range of the related code. May point to a different file than the owning diagnostic. |\n| `message`  | `string`   | Human-readable description of the relationship. |\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property   | Type       | Description |\n|------------|------------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location (URI + range) of this related information. |\n| `message`  | `string`   | The message describing the relationship. |\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- `DiagnosticRelatedInformation` instances are attached to a `Diagnostic` via `diagnostic.relatedInformation`.\n- The `location` can reference a completely different file from the owning diagnostic, enabling cross-file diagnostic context.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticTag`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nAdditional metadata tags for categorizing diagnostics. Tags affect how diagnostics are rendered in the editor.\n\n| Member        | Value | Description |\n|---------------|-------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | `1`   | Unused or unnecessary code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered faded out. The opacity is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color (e.g., `\"#000000c0\"` = 75% opacity). For high-contrast themes, `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` underlines the code instead. |\n| `Deprecated`  | `2`   | Deprecated or obsolete code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered with a strikethrough. |\n\nMultiple tags may be combined on a single diagnostic. Tags are independent of severity; a deprecated warning is represented as `severity: Warning, tags: [DiagnosticTag.Deprecated]`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticChangeEvent`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nThe event object passed to subscribers of `onDidChangeDiagnostics`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type              | Description |\n|----------|-------------------|-------------|\n| `uris`   | `readonly Uri[]`  | Array of resource URIs for which diagnostics have changed. URIs are deduplicated even if multiple collections changed diagnostics for the same URI. |\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### `createDiagnosticCollection()`\n\n**Namespace:** `vscode.languages`\n\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection;\n```\n\nCreates and returns a new `DiagnosticCollection`.\n\n| Parameter | Type     | Required | Description |\n|-----------|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `name`    | `string` | No       | The name of the collection, used to identify the source in the Problems panel and for task problem matchers. |\n\n**Return value:** A new `DiagnosticCollection` instance.\n\n**Behavior notes:**\n\n- If `name` is omitted, a unique auto-generated name is used internally (e.g., `_generated_diagnostic_collection_name_#0`).\n- If a collection with the given `name` already exists (from a previous call), a warning is logged and the new collection receives a unique internal owner name (e.g., `myname0`, `myname1`). The `name` property of the returned collection still returns the requested name.\n- The returned collection must be disposed when no longer needed (e.g., in `ExtensionContext.subscriptions` or via explicit `dispose()`).\n- Creating a collection does **not** automatically push it to `ExtensionContext.subscriptions`. That must be done explicitly.\n\n---\n\n### `getDiagnostics()`\n\n**Namespace:** `vscode.languages`\n\nTwo overloads are available:\n\n```typescript\n// Get diagnostics for a specific resource\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[];\n\n// Get all diagnostics across the entire workspace\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][];\n```\n\n**Single-resource overload:**\n\n| Parameter  | Type  | Description |\n|------------|-------|-------------|\n| `resource` | `Uri` | The file URI to query. |\n\n**Return value:** An array of `Diagnostic` objects for the specified resource, aggregated from **all** registered diagnostic collections. Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist for the resource.\n\n**No-argument overload:**\n\n**Return value:** An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples covering all resources that have diagnostics. Each URI appears at most once; diagnostics from multiple collections for the same URI are merged into a single array.\n\n**Behavior notes:**\n\n- Results include diagnostics from all collections (all extensions), not just the caller's own collection.\n- The returned diagnostics are a snapshot; changes to collections after this call are not reflected.\n- The no-argument form returns an empty array (not `undefined`) if no diagnostics exist anywhere.\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### `onDidChangeDiagnostics`\n\n**Namespace:** `vscode.languages`\n\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\nAn event that fires whenever the global set of diagnostics changes\u2014including additions, updates, and removals from any diagnostic collection of any extension.\n\n**Event data:** `DiagnosticChangeEvent` \u2014 contains `uris`, an array of the resource URIs whose diagnostics changed.\n\n**Firing behavior:**\n\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.set()` is called (even if data is unchanged).\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.delete()` is called.\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.clear()` is called (once, with all URIs in the collection).\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.dispose()` is called (with all URIs that had diagnostics).\n- The event is debounced with a ~50 ms delay; multiple rapid changes are batched into a single event. URIs are deduplicated across batched calls.\n- The `uris` array contains only the URIs that were actually modified, not all URIs with diagnostics.\n\n**Usage:** Subscribe via `vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(handler)`. The subscription returns a `Disposable` that should be stored and disposed when the subscription is no longer needed.\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Linting on Save\n\nCreates a diagnostic collection, validates a document on save, and cleans up when the document is closed.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.workspace.onDidSaveTextDocument(document => {\n            if (document.languageId === 'plaintext') {\n                validateDocument(document, collection);\n            }\n        })\n    );\n\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(document => {\n            collection.delete(document.uri);\n        })\n    );\n}\n\nfunction validateDocument(\n    document: vscode.TextDocument,\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection\n): void {\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n        const line = document.lineAt(i);\n        if (line.text.length > 120) {\n            const range = new vscode.Range(i, 120, i, line.text.length);\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                range,\n                `Line exceeds 120 characters (${line.text.length})`,\n                vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\n            diagnostic.code = 'line-too-long';\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n    }\n\n    collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Related Information and Tags\n\nShows how to use `DiagnosticRelatedInformation` for cross-reference context and `DiagnosticTag` for visual styling.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nfunction reportDuplicateSymbol(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    duplicateUri: vscode.Uri,\n    duplicateRange: vscode.Range,\n    originalUri: vscode.Uri,\n    originalRange: vscode.Range\n): void {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        duplicateRange,\n        'Duplicate symbol declaration',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n    );\n\n    diagnostic.source = 'my-language-server';\n    diagnostic.code = { value: 'E001', target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://docs.example.com/errors/E001') };\n\n    // Point to the original declaration\n    diagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n        new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n            new vscode.Location(originalUri, originalRange),\n            'First declared here'\n        )\n    ];\n\n    collection.set(duplicateUri, [diagnostic]);\n}\n\nfunction reportUnusedVariable(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    uri: vscode.Uri,\n    range: vscode.Range,\n    name: string\n): void {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        `'${name}' is declared but never used`,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n    );\n\n    diagnostic.source = 'my-language-server';\n    diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary]; // renders faded out\n    collection.set(uri, [diagnostic]);\n}\n\nfunction reportDeprecatedApi(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    uri: vscode.Uri,\n    range: vscode.Range,\n    apiName: string\n): void {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        `'${apiName}' is deprecated`,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n    );\n\n    diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated]; // renders with strikethrough\n    collection.set(uri, [diagnostic]);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Subscribing to Diagnostic Changes\n\nReacts to changes in diagnostics across the workspace.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n            for (const uri of event.uris) {\n                const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n                const errors = diagnostics.filter(\n                    d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n                );\n                if (errors.length > 0) {\n                    console.log(`${uri.fsPath} has ${errors.length} error(s)`);\n                }\n            }\n        })\n    );\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Bulk Update with Multiple Resources\n\nUses the array form of `set()` to update diagnostics for multiple files atomically.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nfunction publishDiagnosticsForWorkspace(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    results: Map<vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]>\n): void {\n    const entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [];\n    for (const [uri, diagnostics] of results) {\n        entries.push([uri, diagnostics]);\n    }\n    // Fires onDidChangeDiagnostics once (debounced) for all changed URIs\n    collection.set(entries);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern: Diagnostic Collection as a Class Member\n\nThe most common pattern is to own the collection as a class field, push it to `subscriptions`, and update it in response to document events.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/extension-editing/src/extensionLinter.ts\nexport class ExtensionLinter {\n    private diagnosticsCollection = languages.createDiagnosticCollection('extension-editing');\n    private disposables: Disposable[] = [this.diagnosticsCollection]; // auto-disposed\n\n    constructor() {\n        this.disposables.push(\n            workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(document => this.queue(document)),\n            workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => this.queue(event.document)),\n            workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(document => this.clear(document)),\n        );\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern: Clearing on Close\n\nAlways delete diagnostics for a document when it is closed to avoid stale entries in the Problems panel.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/php-language-features/src/features/validationProvider.ts\nvscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(textDocument => {\n    this.diagnosticCollection!.delete(textDocument.uri);\n}, null, subscriptions);\n```\n\n### Pattern: Conditional Clear\n\nUse `set(uri, undefined)` to signal \"no diagnostics\" when validation produces no results.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/git/src/diagnostics.ts\nif (!inputValidation) {\n    this.diagnostics.set(document.uri, undefined); // removes diagnostics\n    return;\n}\n// ... otherwise build and publish diagnostics\nthis.diagnostics.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n```\n\n### Pattern: Iterating the Collection\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` implements `Iterable`, enabling `for...of` loops and also exposing a `forEach` method.\n\n```typescript\n// Using for...of (via Symbol.iterator)\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    console.log(uri.toString(), diagnostics.length);\n}\n\n// Using forEach\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, col) => {\n    console.log(uri.toString(), diagnostics.length);\n});\n```\n\n### Pattern: Reading Diagnostics from Your Own Collection\n\nUse `collection.get(uri)` for diagnostics you own (faster, collection-scoped) rather than `languages.getDiagnostics(uri)`, which aggregates all collections.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/git/src/diagnostics.ts\npublic getDiagnostics(uri: Uri): ReadonlyArray<Diagnostic> {\n    return this.diagnostics.get(uri) ?? [];\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern: Using `DiagnosticCollection` with the Task Framework\n\nWhen the collection name matches a problem matcher's owner, the VS Code task framework integrates output markers from task runners with the Diagnostic API. Set the `name` parameter to the same string used in the problem matcher definition.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### After Disposal\n\nAll `DiagnosticCollection` methods (except `dispose()` itself, which is idempotent) throw `Error: illegal state - object is disposed` when called after the collection has been disposed.\n\n```typescript\ncollection.dispose();\ncollection.dispose(); // safe, no-op\ncollection.clear();   // throws Error\ncollection.name;      // throws Error\n```\n\n**Recommendation:** Push the collection to `context.subscriptions` so VS Code automatically disposes it on extension deactivation. Do not call `dispose()` manually unless the collection is meant to have a shorter lifetime.\n\n### Duplicate Collection Names\n\nIf `createDiagnosticCollection(name)` is called with a name already in use, a warning is logged (`DiagnosticCollection with name 'X' does already exist.`) and the new collection gets a unique internal owner (e.g., `name0`). Its `name` property still returns the requested name. This does not throw.\n\n### Immutable Arrays from `get()`\n\nThe array returned by `collection.get(uri)` is frozen. Any attempt to modify it throws a `TypeError`:\n\n```typescript\nconst diags = collection.get(uri); // returns frozen array\ndiags.push(newDiag);               // throws TypeError\n```\n\nTo update, build a new array and call `set()`:\n\n```typescript\nconst existing = [...(collection.get(uri) ?? [])];\nexisting.push(newDiag);\ncollection.set(uri, existing);\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Construction Errors\n\nThe `Diagnostic` constructor throws `TypeError` in two cases:\n\n- `range` is not a valid `Range`: `'range must be set'`\n- `message` is empty or falsy: `'message must be set'`\n\n### Per-file and Total Diagnostic Limits\n\nVS Code enforces the following limits:\n\n- **Per file:** 1000 diagnostics maximum. When exceeded, diagnostics are truncated by severity (Errors preserved first), and an informational marker is appended: `\"Not showing N further errors and warnings.\"`\n- **Total across collection:** ~1100 diagnostics maximum. Files are processed in `set()` order; once the total is exceeded, remaining files are skipped.\n\nThese limits are imposed by the extension host's internal `DiagnosticCollection` implementation and apply transparently.\n",

  "content": "# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe VS Code Diagnostic API enables extensions to report code issues\u2014errors, warnings, informational messages, and hints\u2014to users within the editor. Diagnostics appear as underlined text in the editor, as entries in the Problems panel, and in the gutter. They are scoped to a specific document URI and managed through diagnostic collections, which group diagnostics by the owning extension or tool.\n\nThe primary entry point is the `vscode.languages` namespace, which provides factory functions and events for working with diagnostics.\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### `Diagnostic`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nRepresents a single diagnostic (error, warning, info, or hint) that applies to a specific range within a document. `Diagnostic` objects are only valid within the scope of a file and must be published via a `DiagnosticCollection` to be visible.\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nconstructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type                | Required | Description |\n|------------|---------------------|----------|-------------|\n| `range`    | `Range`             | Yes      | The range in the document to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid `Range`; throws `TypeError` if not. |\n| `message`  | `string`            | Yes      | The human-readable message to display. Must be non-empty; throws `TypeError` if falsy. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity`| No       | The severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n\n**Error cases:** The constructor throws `TypeError` if `range` is not a valid `Range` or if `message` is empty/falsy.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property             | Type                                                                          | Description |\n|----------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------|\n| `range`              | `Range`                                                                       | The document range the diagnostic applies to. |\n| `message`            | `string`                                                                      | The human-readable diagnostic message. |\n| `severity`           | `DiagnosticSeverity`                                                          | Severity level; defaults to `Error`. |\n| `source`             | `string \\| undefined`                                                         | Optional human-readable source name, e.g. `'typescript'` or `'eslint'`. Used to identify the originating tool in the Problems panel. |\n| `code`               | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri } \\| undefined`  | Optional code or identifier. When an object form is used, `target` is a URI opened when the user clicks the diagnostic code for more information. |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[] \\| undefined`                                 | Optional array of related locations and messages (e.g., other definitions of a duplicate symbol). |\n| `tags`               | `DiagnosticTag[] \\| undefined`                                                | Optional metadata tags that affect rendering (e.g., fading out unnecessary code). |\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- A `Diagnostic` instance has no visual effect until it is added to a `DiagnosticCollection` via `set()`.\n- The `range` does not have to be non-empty; a zero-length range (a cursor position) is valid.\n- `null` diagnostic values inside an array passed to `DiagnosticCollection.set()` are silently coalesced (filtered out).\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticCollection`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nA container that manages a named set of diagnostics across multiple document URIs. Created exclusively via `languages.createDiagnosticCollection()`. Implements `Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]>`, so it can be iterated with `for...of`.\n\nEach diagnostic collection is associated with a single owning extension. Diagnostics from different collections for the same URI are aggregated when calling `languages.getDiagnostics()`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type     | Description |\n|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `name`   | `string` (readonly) | The collection name, set at creation time. Every diagnostic from this collection is associated with this name. Also used by the task framework for problem matchers. Throws if accessed after `dispose()`. |\n\n#### Methods\n\n##### `set(uri, diagnostics)`\n\n```typescript\nset(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n```\n\nAssigns diagnostics for a single resource, replacing all existing diagnostics for that URI.\n\n| Parameter     | Type                                | Description |\n|---------------|-------------------------------------|-------------|\n| `uri`         | `Uri`                               | The resource to update. |\n| `diagnostics` | `readonly Diagnostic[] \\| undefined`| New diagnostics, or `undefined` to remove all diagnostics for that URI (equivalent to `delete(uri)`). |\n\n##### `set(entries)`\n\n```typescript\nset(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n```\n\nReplaces diagnostics for multiple resources in one call.\n\n| Parameter | Type | Description |\n|-----------|------|-------------|\n| `entries` | `ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] \\| undefined]>` | Array of `[uri, diagnostics]` tuples. |\n\n**Merge semantics:** Multiple tuples with the same URI are merged. For example, `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` is equivalent to `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`. A `undefined` diagnostics entry (e.g., `[file1, undefined]`) clears all diagnostics accumulated for `file1` up to that point in the array, but subsequent tuples for the same URI can still add diagnostics.\n\n**Behavior notes:**\n- Calling `set()` always fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` for the affected URIs, even if the diagnostic content has not actually changed.\n- `null` entries within a diagnostics array are silently filtered out.\n- There is a per-file limit (1000 diagnostics) and a total limit (~1100 diagnostics). When a file exceeds the per-file limit, diagnostics are prioritized by severity (Errors first, then Warnings, then Information, then Hints), and an additional informational marker is appended indicating how many diagnostics were omitted.\n- Throws `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `delete(uri)`\n\n```typescript\ndelete(uri: Uri): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics for the given URI from this collection. Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `clear()`\n\n```typescript\nclear(): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics from this collection for every URI. Equivalent to calling `set(undefined)`.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `forEach(callback, thisArg?)`\n\n```typescript\nforEach(\n  callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n  thisArg?: any\n): void\n```\n\nIterates over each URI/diagnostics entry in this collection.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `get(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nget(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n```\n\nReturns the diagnostics for the given URI, or `undefined` if none exist.\n\n**Important:** The returned array is immutable (frozen). Attempting to mutate it (e.g., `push`, `pop`, index assignment) throws a `TypeError`. To modify diagnostics, create a new array and call `set()` again.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `has(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nhas(uri: Uri): boolean\n```\n\nReturns `true` if this collection contains any diagnostics for the given URI.\n\nThrows `Error` if called after `dispose()`.\n\n##### `dispose()`\n\n```typescript\ndispose(): void\n```\n\nDisposes the collection and frees associated resources. Internally calls `clear()`, removing all diagnostics from the editor. Calling `dispose()` a second time is safe (no-op). After disposal, all other methods throw `Error: illegal state - object is disposed`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticSeverity`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nEnum representing the severity level of a diagnostic. Controls how the diagnostic is rendered in the editor and Problems panel.\n\n| Member        | Value | Description |\n|---------------|-------|-------------|\n| `Error`       | `0`   | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Rendered with a red underline by default. |\n| `Warning`     | `1`   | Something suspicious but allowed. Rendered with a yellow underline by default. |\n| `Information` | `2`   | Something to inform about but not a problem. |\n| `Hint`        | `3`   | A suggestion for a better approach (e.g., proposing a refactoring). Rendered subtly. |\n\n**Priority ordering:** When per-file diagnostic limits are reached, diagnostics are preserved in order: `Error` > `Warning` > `Information` > `Hint`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticRelatedInformation`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nRepresents a related message and source location for a diagnostic. Used to point to code locations that cause or are related to the diagnostic, such as all definitions of a duplicated symbol.\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nconstructor(location: Location, message: string)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type       | Description |\n|------------|------------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The file and range of the related code. May point to a different file than the owning diagnostic. |\n| `message`  | `string`   | Human-readable description of the relationship. |\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property   | Type       | Description |\n|------------|------------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location (URI + range) of this related information. |\n| `message`  | `string`   | The message describing the relationship. |\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- `DiagnosticRelatedInformation` instances are attached to a `Diagnostic` via `diagnostic.relatedInformation`.\n- The `location` can reference a completely different file from the owning diagnostic, enabling cross-file diagnostic context.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticTag`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nAdditional metadata tags for categorizing diagnostics. Tags affect how diagnostics are rendered in the editor.\n\n| Member        | Value | Description |\n|---------------|-------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | `1`   | Unused or unnecessary code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered faded out. The opacity is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color (e.g., `\"#000000c0\"` = 75% opacity). For high-contrast themes, `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` underlines the code instead. |\n| `Deprecated`  | `2`   | Deprecated or obsolete code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered with a strikethrough. |\n\nMultiple tags may be combined on a single diagnostic. Tags are independent of severity; a deprecated warning is represented as `severity: Warning, tags: [DiagnosticTag.Deprecated]`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticChangeEvent`\n\n**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`\n\nThe event object passed to subscribers of `onDidChangeDiagnostics`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type              | Description |\n|----------|-------------------|-------------|\n| `uris`   | `readonly Uri[]`  | Array of resource URIs for which diagnostics have changed. URIs are deduplicated even if multiple collections changed diagnostics for the same URI. |\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### `createDiagnosticCollection()`\n\n**Namespace:** `vscode.languages`\n\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection;\n```\n\nCreates and returns a new `DiagnosticCollection`.\n\n| Parameter | Type     | Required | Description |\n|-----------|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `name`    | `string` | No       | The name of the collection, used to identify the source in the Problems panel and for task problem matchers. |\n\n**Return value:** A new `DiagnosticCollection` instance.\n\n**Behavior notes:**\n\n- If `name` is omitted, a unique auto-generated name is used internally (e.g., `_generated_diagnostic_collection_name_#0`).\n- If a collection with the given `name` already exists (from a previous call), a warning is logged and the new collection receives a unique internal owner name (e.g., `myname0`, `myname1`). The `name` property of the returned collection still returns the requested name.\n- The returned collection must be disposed when no longer needed (e.g., in `ExtensionContext.subscriptions` or via explicit `dispose()`).\n- Creating a collection does **not** automatically push it to `ExtensionContext.subscriptions`. That must be done explicitly.\n\n---\n\n### `getDiagnostics()`\n\n**Namespace:** `vscode.languages`\n\nTwo overloads are available:\n\n```typescript\n// Get diagnostics for a specific resource\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[];\n\n// Get all diagnostics across the entire workspace\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][];\n```\n\n**Single-resource overload:**\n\n| Parameter  | Type  | Description |\n|------------|-------|-------------|\n| `resource` | `Uri` | The file URI to query. |\n\n**Return value:** An array of `Diagnostic` objects for the specified resource, aggregated from **all** registered diagnostic collections. Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist for the resource.\n\n**No-argument overload:**\n\n**Return value:** An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples covering all resources that have diagnostics. Each URI appears at most once; diagnostics from multiple collections for the same URI are merged into a single array.\n\n**Behavior notes:**\n\n- Results include diagnostics from all collections (all extensions), not just the caller's own collection.\n- The returned diagnostics are a snapshot; changes to collections after this call are not reflected.\n- The no-argument form returns an empty array (not `undefined`) if no diagnostics exist anywhere.\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### `onDidChangeDiagnostics`\n\n**Namespace:** `vscode.languages`\n\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\nAn event that fires whenever the global set of diagnostics changes\u2014including additions, updates, and removals from any diagnostic collection of any extension.\n\n**Event data:** `DiagnosticChangeEvent` \u2014 contains `uris`, an array of the resource URIs whose diagnostics changed.\n\n**Firing behavior:**\n\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.set()` is called (even if data is unchanged).\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.delete()` is called.\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.clear()` is called (once, with all URIs in the collection).\n- Fires when `DiagnosticCollection.dispose()` is called (with all URIs that had diagnostics).\n- The event is debounced with a ~50 ms delay; multiple rapid changes are batched into a single event. URIs are deduplicated across batched calls.\n- The `uris` array contains only the URIs that were actually modified, not all URIs with diagnostics.\n\n**Usage:** Subscribe via `vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(handler)`. The subscription returns a `Disposable` that should be stored and disposed when the subscription is no longer needed.\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Linting on Save\n\nCreates a diagnostic collection, validates a document on save, and cleans up when the document is closed.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.workspace.onDidSaveTextDocument(document => {\n            if (document.languageId === 'plaintext') {\n                validateDocument(document, collection);\n            }\n        })\n    );\n\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(document => {\n            collection.delete(document.uri);\n        })\n    );\n}\n\nfunction validateDocument(\n    document: vscode.TextDocument,\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection\n): void {\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n        const line = document.lineAt(i);\n        if (line.text.length > 120) {\n            const range = new vscode.Range(i, 120, i, line.text.length);\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                range,\n                `Line exceeds 120 characters (${line.text.length})`,\n                vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\n            diagnostic.code = 'line-too-long';\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n    }\n\n    collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Related Information and Tags\n\nShows how to use `DiagnosticRelatedInformation` for cross-reference context and `DiagnosticTag` for visual styling.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nfunction reportDuplicateSymbol(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    duplicateUri: vscode.Uri,\n    duplicateRange: vscode.Range,\n    originalUri: vscode.Uri,\n    originalRange: vscode.Range\n): void {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        duplicateRange,\n        'Duplicate symbol declaration',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n    );\n\n    diagnostic.source = 'my-language-server';\n    diagnostic.code = { value: 'E001', target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://docs.example.com/errors/E001') };\n\n    // Point to the original declaration\n    diagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n        new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n            new vscode.Location(originalUri, originalRange),\n            'First declared here'\n        )\n    ];\n\n    collection.set(duplicateUri, [diagnostic]);\n}\n\nfunction reportUnusedVariable(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    uri: vscode.Uri,\n    range: vscode.Range,\n    name: string\n): void {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        `'${name}' is declared but never used`,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n    );\n\n    diagnostic.source = 'my-language-server';\n    diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary]; // renders faded out\n    collection.set(uri, [diagnostic]);\n}\n\nfunction reportDeprecatedApi(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    uri: vscode.Uri,\n    range: vscode.Range,\n    apiName: string\n): void {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        `'${apiName}' is deprecated`,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n    );\n\n    diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated]; // renders with strikethrough\n    collection.set(uri, [diagnostic]);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Subscribing to Diagnostic Changes\n\nReacts to changes in diagnostics across the workspace.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n            for (const uri of event.uris) {\n                const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n                const errors = diagnostics.filter(\n                    d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n                );\n                if (errors.length > 0) {\n                    console.log(`${uri.fsPath} has ${errors.length} error(s)`);\n                }\n            }\n        })\n    );\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Bulk Update with Multiple Resources\n\nUses the array form of `set()` to update diagnostics for multiple files atomically.\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nfunction publishDiagnosticsForWorkspace(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    results: Map<vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]>\n): void {\n    const entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [];\n    for (const [uri, diagnostics] of results) {\n        entries.push([uri, diagnostics]);\n    }\n    // Fires onDidChangeDiagnostics once (debounced) for all changed URIs\n    collection.set(entries);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern: Diagnostic Collection as a Class Member\n\nThe most common pattern is to own the collection as a class field, push it to `subscriptions`, and update it in response to document events.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/extension-editing/src/extensionLinter.ts\nexport class ExtensionLinter {\n    private diagnosticsCollection = languages.createDiagnosticCollection('extension-editing');\n    private disposables: Disposable[] = [this.diagnosticsCollection]; // auto-disposed\n\n    constructor() {\n        this.disposables.push(\n            workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(document => this.queue(document)),\n            workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => this.queue(event.document)),\n            workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(document => this.clear(document)),\n        );\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern: Clearing on Close\n\nAlways delete diagnostics for a document when it is closed to avoid stale entries in the Problems panel.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/php-language-features/src/features/validationProvider.ts\nvscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(textDocument => {\n    this.diagnosticCollection!.delete(textDocument.uri);\n}, null, subscriptions);\n```\n\n### Pattern: Conditional Clear\n\nUse `set(uri, undefined)` to signal \"no diagnostics\" when validation produces no results.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/git/src/diagnostics.ts\nif (!inputValidation) {\n    this.diagnostics.set(document.uri, undefined); // removes diagnostics\n    return;\n}\n// ... otherwise build and publish diagnostics\nthis.diagnostics.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n```\n\n### Pattern: Iterating the Collection\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` implements `Iterable`, enabling `for...of` loops and also exposing a `forEach` method.\n\n```typescript\n// Using for...of (via Symbol.iterator)\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    console.log(uri.toString(), diagnostics.length);\n}\n\n// Using forEach\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, col) => {\n    console.log(uri.toString(), diagnostics.length);\n});\n```\n\n### Pattern: Reading Diagnostics from Your Own Collection\n\nUse `collection.get(uri)` for diagnostics you own (faster, collection-scoped) rather than `languages.getDiagnostics(uri)`, which aggregates all collections.\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/git/src/diagnostics.ts\npublic getDiagnostics(uri: Uri): ReadonlyArray<Diagnostic> {\n    return this.diagnostics.get(uri) ?? [];\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern: Using `DiagnosticCollection` with the Task Framework\n\nWhen the collection name matches a problem matcher's owner, the VS Code task framework integrates output markers from task runners with the Diagnostic API. Set the `name` parameter to the same string used in the problem matcher definition.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### After Disposal\n\nAll `DiagnosticCollection` methods (except `dispose()` itself, which is idempotent) throw `Error: illegal state - object is disposed` when called after the collection has been disposed.\n\n```typescript\ncollection.dispose();\ncollection.dispose(); // safe, no-op\ncollection.clear();   // throws Error\ncollection.name;      // throws Error\n```\n\n**Recommendation:** Push the collection to `context.subscriptions` so VS Code automatically disposes it on extension deactivation. Do not call `dispose()` manually unless the collection is meant to have a shorter lifetime.\n\n### Duplicate Collection Names\n\nIf `createDiagnosticCollection(name)` is called with a name already in use, a warning is logged (`DiagnosticCollection with name 'X' does already exist.`) and the new collection gets a unique internal owner (e.g., `name0`). Its `name` property still returns the requested name. This does not throw.\n\n### Immutable Arrays from `get()`\n\nThe array returned by `collection.get(uri)` is frozen. Any attempt to modify it throws a `TypeError`:\n\n```typescript\nconst diags = collection.get(uri); // returns frozen array\ndiags.push(newDiag);               // throws TypeError\n```\n\nTo update, build a new array and call `set()`:\n\n```typescript\nconst existing = [...(collection.get(uri) ?? [])];\nexisting.push(newDiag);\ncollection.set(uri, existing);\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Construction Errors\n\nThe `Diagnostic` constructor throws `TypeError` in two cases:\n\n- `range` is not a valid `Range`: `'range must be set'`\n- `message` is empty or falsy: `'message must be set'`\n\n### Per-file and Total Diagnostic Limits\n\nVS Code enforces the following limits:\n\n- **Per file:** 1000 diagnostics maximum. When exceeded, diagnostics are truncated by severity (Errors preserved first), and an informational marker is appended: `\"Not showing N further errors and warnings.\"`\n- **Total across collection:** ~1100 diagnostics maximum. Files are processed in `set()` order; once the total is exceeded, remaining files are skipped.\n\nThese limits are imposed by the extension host's internal `DiagnosticCollection` implementation and apply transparently.\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/documentation.md
# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference

## Overview

The VS Code Diagnostic API enables extensions to report code issues—errors, warnings, informational messages, and hints—to users within the editor. Diagnostics appear as underlined text in the editor, as entries in the Problems panel, and in the gutter. They are scoped to a specific document URI and managed through diagnostic collections, which group diagnostics by the owning extension or tool.

The primary entry point is the `vscode.languages` namespace, which provides factory functions and events for working with diagnostics.

---

## Core Types

### `Diagnostic`

**File:** `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`

Represents a single diagnostic (error, warning, info, or hint) that applies to a specific range within a document. `Diagnostic` objects are only valid within the scope of a file and must be published via a `DiagnosticCollection` to be visible.

#### Constructor

```typescript
constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)
```

| Parameter  | Type                | Required | Description |
|------------|---------------------|----------|-------------|
| `range`    | `Range`             | Yes      | The range in the document to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid `Range`; throws `TypeError` if not. |
| `message`  | `string`            | Yes      | The human-readable message to display. Must be non-empty; throws `TypeError` if falsy. |
| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity`| No       | The severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |

**Error cases:** The constructor throws `TypeError` if `range` is not a valid `Range` or if `message` is empty/falsy.

| Property             | Type                                                                          | Descrip
... (truncated)
